Dec 7, 2023

Animated SVGs

The Format

The main benefit of SVGs (Scalable Vector Graphics) is in the name. Unlike shitty raster formats like PNG and JPEG, vector graphics don’t care where they are or how big they need to be, they just work (at scale btw).

There is nothing SVGs can’t do that rasters think they excel at. And they have to create specific formats for every use-case just to keep up. PNG for transparency, JPEG for quality and GIF for fighting about pronounciation (and creating animations) blablabla who cares? Have you ever tried to read a TIFF? Here is their logo:

⬆ Oh what’s that, you can’t see anything here? Well then I guess you must be on literally any other browser than Safari (on day of posting). Here is a PNG for you poor people.

Pretty terrible isn’t it? Not just reading bytecode; they trademarked this? Anyway, its so terrible in fact, that they themselves used another format to create it. Can you guess which one? You guessed it. Here it is in all its glory:

One of the greatest things about SVGs is the ability to directly change the graphical representation by manipulating the markup. Here is an example of making the I in the TIFF logo cursive using this straight-forward method.

1. Finding the I 📑

Looking at the markdown we can assume the second path is the second letter.

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<svg width="400pt" height="122.59pt" version="1.1" viewBox="0 0 400 122.59" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">
 <g transform="matrix(2.854 0 0 2.854 -721.47 -513.85)">
  <g transform="translate(251.5, 223)">
   <path d="m14.031 0v-35.688h-12.734v-7.2656h34.125v7.2656h-12.719v35.688z"/>
  </g>
  <g transform="translate(288.16, 223)">
-> <path d="m4.1094 0v-42.953h8.6719v42.953z"/>
  </g>
  <g transform="translate(304.84, 223)">
   <path d="m4.4219 0v-42.953h29.453v7.2656h-20.781v10.172h17.938v7.2656h-17.938v18.25z"/>
  </g>

  </g>
 </g>
</svg>

2. Curving the I 🌊

Knowing CSS, the next part should be easy. We just set the font-style to italic!

Well actually 🤓, that makes sense. Because the I itself is not a character, it’s a blablabla™. Nothing a transform can’t fix!

3. Advanced Styles 👨‍🎨

Now before we get to the really juicy part of this article, we have to take a quick look at how to webify the SVG workflow.

Using the <style> tag we can use scoped styles like in your favourite UI frlibrarwork™ (thanks React). And yes that is an SVG.

Here’s an example of what I’m talking about:

<div style="display: flex; justify-content: center">
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<svg width="400pt" height="122.59pt" version="1.1" viewBox="0 0 400 122.59" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">
+  <style>
+   .blue {
+     fill: blue;
+    }
+  </style>
+ <g class="blue">
   <g transform="matrix(2.854 0 0 2.854 -721.47 -513.85)">
    <g transform="translate(251.5, 223)">
     <path d="m14.031 0v-35.688h-12.734v-7.2656h34.125v7.  2656h-12.719v35.688z"/>
    </g>
    <g transform="translate(288.16, 223)">
   <path
    d="m4.1094 0v-42.953h8.6719v42.953z"
   />
    </g>
    <g transform="translate(304.84, 223)">
     <path d="m4.4219 0v-42.953h29.453v7.2656h-20.781v10.  172h17.938v7.2656h-17.938v18.25z"/>
    </g>
    <g transform="translate(341.5, 223)">
     <path d="m4.4219 0v-42.953h29.453v7.2656h-20.781v10.  172h17.938v7.2656h-17.938v18.25z"/>
    </g>
    <g transform="translate(382.5, 190)">
     <path d="m2.8594-3.8125v-4.0625h-1.5469v-0.71875h3.  9062v0.71875h-1.5625v4.0625zm2.8906 0v-4.7812h1.1719l1.  2188 3.8125 1.1562-3.8125h1.1562v4.7812h-0.73438v-4.  0156l-1.2344 4.0156h-0.71875l-1.2812-4.0625v4.0625z"/>
    </g>
   </g>
+ </g>
</svg>
</div>


We added a <style> tag to the top of the SVG, and wrapped the <path> tags with a <g class="blue">. The <g> tag adds its attributes to its children.

Advanced Styles Advanced Styles

Animations

Meanwhile over at GIF headquarters:

Now that we have mastered reading and directly manipulating the SVG markup, we can graduate to what some would call the best feature of SVGs, the intuitive animation syntax.

Using what we have learned so far you might have had the idea to do something like:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<svg width="400pt" height="122.59pt" version="1.1" viewBox="0 0 400 122.59" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">
<style>
 .flash {
  animation: 3s flash infinite;
 }
 @keyframes flash {
  0%, 100% {
   opacity: 0;
  }
  50% {
   opacity: 1
  }
 }
</style>
<g class="flash">
 <g transform="matrix(2.854 0 0 2.854 -721.47 -513.85)">
  <g transform="translate(251.5, 223)">
   <path d="m14.031 0v-35.688h-12.734v-7.2656h34.125v7.2656h-12.719v35.688z"/>
  </g>
  <g transform="translate(288.16, 223)">
 <path
  d="m4.1094 0v-42.953h8.6719v42.953z"
 />
  </g>
  <g transform="translate(304.84, 223)">
   <path d="m4.4219 0v-42.953h29.453v7.2656h-20.781v10.172h17.938v7.2656h-17.938v18.25z"/>
  </g>
  <g transform="translate(341.5, 223)">
   <path d="m4.4219 0v-42.953h29.453v7.2656h-20.781v10.172h17.938v7.2656h-17.938v18.25z"/>
  </g>
  <g transform="translate(382.5, 190)">
   <path d="m2.8594-3.8125v-4.0625h-1.5469v-0.71875h3.9062v0.71875h-1.5625v4.0625zm2.8906 0v-4.7812h1.1719l1.2188 3.8125 1.1562-3.8125h1.1562v4.7812h-0.73438v-4.0156l-1.2344 4.0156h-0.71875l-1.2812-4.0625v4.0625z"/>
  </g>
 </g>
</g>
</svg>

Which would result in:


Animations 🏃‍♂️ It works WOO! 🛑 STOP, not so fast! 🛑

The keenest 🦅 readers, would have noticed the <animate> tag in the previous section. The rest of you who didn’t, should feel bad (go un-tick the ‘Tis But a Scratch).

Anyway, animations in SVG work similarily to CSS but with a sexy syntax ™.

Here it is re-written the correct way:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<svg width="400pt" height="122.59pt" version="1.1" viewBox="0 0 400 122.59" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">
<g>
 <animate
  attributeName="opacity"
  values="0;1;0"
  dur="2s"
  repeatCount="indefinite"
 />
 <g transform="matrix(2.854 0 0 2.854 -721.47 -513.85)">
  <g transform="translate(251.5, 223)">
   <path d="m14.031 0v-35.688h-12.734v-7.2656h34.125v7.2656h-12.719v35.688z"/>
  </g>
  <g transform="translate(288.16, 223)">
 <path
  d="m4.1094 0v-42.953h8.6719v42.953z"
 />
  </g>
  <g transform="translate(304.84, 223)">
   <path d="m4.4219 0v-42.953h29.453v7.2656h-20.781v10.172h17.938v7.2656h-17.938v18.25z"/>
  </g>
  <g transform="translate(341.5, 223)">
   <path d="m4.4219 0v-42.953h29.453v7.2656h-20.781v10.172h17.938v7.2656h-17.938v18.25z"/>
  </g>
  <g transform="translate(382.5, 190)">
   <path d="m2.8594-3.8125v-4.0625h-1.5469v-0.71875h3.9062v0.71875h-1.5625v4.0625zm2.8906 0v-4.7812h1.1719l1.2188 3.8125 1.1562-3.8125h1.1562v4.7812h-0.73438v-4.0156l-1.2344 4.0156h-0.71875l-1.2812-4.0625v4.0625z"/>
  </g>
 </g>
</g>
</svg>


We swapped out the <style> tag but kept the <g> wrapper which has another trick up its sleeve 🃏. Inside the wrapper we add the <animate> tag and recreate the animation with the sexy syntax ™. Transformations on <g> tags are also applied to its children so we only have to define it once!

Animations
